petition, which led the governor to sign a law banning FGM/C. ","photo_id":220640392,"media_url":"https://www.telegram.com/news/20200130/advocates-push-for-anti-female-genital-mutilation-law-mass-one-of-15-states-without-protections","media_text":"Worcester Telegram","video":null,"petition":{"id":13211901,"document_id":"13211901","ask":"Ban Female Genital Mutilation/Cutting in Massachusetts","created_at":"2018-05-23T15:20:08Z","deleted_at":null,"published_at":"2018-05-23T15:20:08Z","last_edited_at":"2020-08-07T14:30:01Z","original_locale":"en-US","languages":["en"],"language_details":{},"title":"Ban Female Genital Mutilation/Cutting in Massachusetts","description":"\u003cp>Our names are Aisha Yusuf, Hanna Stern, and Mariya Taher, and we each are pleading to the Massachusetts State Legislature to pass a law making it illegal for someone to carry out Female Genital Mutilation/Cutting/Circumcision (FGM/C) on young girls.\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>FGM/C involves removing and damaging healthy and normal female genital tissue on girls, and can cause physical harm including pain, bleeding, shock, tetanus, genital sores, and cause long-lasting psychological harm including sexual disorders, fear of sexual intimacy, nightmares and post-traumatic stress disorder.\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>Mariya - I was born in the United States and now live in Massachusetts, but at the age of seven, I was subjected to Female Genital Mutilation/Cutting in India. Friends and relatives of mine also living in the United States have undergone FGM/C both here in the United States or in India, Pakistan, Sri Lanka, Somalia, Australia, and many other countries in the world.\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>Aisha- I got my circumcision when I was five. I know many women who also got it done. Personally, I know people in my community who talk about it as if it’s normal. I was aware of people practicing it behind closed doors but I also know that some people are looking for ways to keep the practice alive here in the States even though it might mean legal action is taken against them. I didn't know my home state, Massachusetts, had no laws against FGM/C until I met Mariya who works with many communities to protect girls against FGM/C.\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>Hanna - I literally stumbled on the subject of female genital mutilation searching for a global health research topic online for a school project. I knew nothing about it and was concerned that others would find it uncomfortable and unrelatable. My teacher told me that was all the more reason to focus on FGM/C. It’s not a cultural issue; it’s not a third-world problem. FGM/C happens all over the world; it is happening in Massachusetts! Regardless of culture and tradition, and despite a lack of intent to cause injury, the end result is girls in MA are being violated and need our protection to safeguard them from FGM/C.\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>Massachusetts is known for its progressive policies in terms of reproductive rights, anti-discrimination laws, and equality issues, yet our state still is in the minority of states that do not ban female genital mutilation or cutting. As FGM/C is nearly always carried out on minors, is a violation of the rights of children, and reflects deep-rooted inequality between the sexes that constitutes an extreme form of discrimination against women, we must protect girls from undergoing FGM/C.\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>According to the Center for Disease Control and Prevention, it is estimated that over half a million girls and women in the United States are at risk. Massachusetts ranks 12th in the nation for at-risk populations with an estimated 14,591 women and girls. \u003c/p>\n\u003cp>Since 2012, the Massachusetts Women’s Bar Association has over and over again tried to advocate for a state law criminalizing FGM/C. Yet, still to this day, no law has been put into place. The current bills, S.788, and H.2333, have been sent to committee for study and most likely will not move forward either.\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>All three of us believe in the importance of education and community engagement to help create social change within communities and amongst groups where FGM/C might be happening. To that end, we each have organized and participated in community events to educate our friends and family members about the harms of FGM/C and why it should be abandoned.\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>Yet, despite our efforts, FGM/C continues, often being touted as a religious or cultural practice that is needed to control women’s sexuality. In April 2017, a doctor in Michigan was charged with performing FGM/C on minor girls, highlighting yet again that FGM/C does affect women and girls living in the United States. The doctor claimed FGM/C was a religious requirement and that there were no harmful effects. We three believe that culture and religion should not be an excuse used to sanction harm to girls.\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>We need a bill in Massachusetts that unequivocally reiterates that female genital mutilation/cutting is a form of violence. There are laws against domestic violence and sexual assault. We need a law against FGM/C as well.\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>We three believe our state can do a better job of protecting girls in the Commonwealth by banning FGM/C.\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>You can support us too by signing our petition demanding that legislators make passing a bill banning FGM/C high on their list of priorities. Let’s work together to take a stance against Female Genital Mutilation/Cutting!\u003c/p>\n\u003cp> ~ Aisha Yusuf, Hanna Stern, and Mariya Taher\u003c/p>","targeting_description":"Charlie Baker, Robert A. We hope you can help with moving the current legislation, \"An Act to Protect Girls from Genital Mutilation\" forward so that this protection will be offered to all girls in Massachusetts.\n\n~ Aisha, Charged with the murder of a white man shot and killed in a Richmond, Virginia apartment complex during a drug deal gone wrong, Rojai turned down plea offer after plea offer — the lowest offer for five years — telling the prosecutor in his case that he was not going to take a plea. He was innocent. Rojai was never interrogated, and his home was never searched. Yet when his case finally went to trial, he was convicted in a trial that lasted just under an hour. \u003c/p>\n\u003cp>In 2014, another man confessed to the murder. The classic log flume ride Splash Mountain is featured in Disneyland, Disney World and Tokyo Disneyland. While the ride is considered a beloved classic it’s history and storyline are steeped in extremely problematic and stereotypical racist tropes from the 1946 film Song of the South.\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>There is a huge need for diversity in the parks and this could help fill that need. Princess and the Frog is a beloved princess movie but has very little representation in the parks. Tiana could be one of the first princesses with a thrill ride, as well as giving her a much deserved place in the parks. The framing of the ride is such that it could be easily changed to tell the story of Tiana while not compromising too much of the ride/costing a fortune in remodeling for Disney. This change could kill two birds with one stone, remove the offensive stereotypical theming the ride currently has and bring a much needed diversity to the parks. As well as a much bigger merchandising opportunity for Princess and the Frog. \u003c/p>\n\u003cp>Splash Mountain is located in Critter Country/Frontierland in the parks, an area very close to New Orleans Square in Disneyland. It would be fairly easy to transition the ride into the bayou of New Orleans considering the location of the ride in each park.\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>While the rides storyline is not an exact version of the movies plot line it is derivative from it, the characters, the songs and locations are all main features of the ride. Disney has removed Song of the South from its library, refusing to share it on DVD or their streaming services. The best next step to remove all traces of this racist movie would be to re-theme Splash Mountain into a Princess and the Frog themed ride. \u003c/p>\n\u003cp>Since this has gotten so much attention I just want to throw in this edit with a few things. I really didn’t think this would get any attention. If you’re willing to have a discussion and potentially educate from a different perspective I appreciate that as well. However this is just a log ride in a theme park, abbeloved one yes, but at the end of the day it’s just a ride, there are more pressing matters in the world currently. passes law to protect young athletes from heat stroke ","description":"Laurie's 16-year-old son died from Exertional Heat Stroke complications during summer football conditioning. She launched a petition to ensure no other mother would lose her child like this – and won. ","photo_id":222856112,"media_url":"https://www.fox13news.com/news/florida-mom-of-high-school-football-player-who-died-of-heatstroke-advocates-for-athlete-safety-bill","media_text":"Fox 13 News ","video":null,"petition":{"id":19467255,"document_id":"19467255","ask":"Support the Zachary Martin Act (Florida Athlete Safety Bill SB1696/HB7011)","created_at":"2019-12-09T19:48:08Z","deleted_at":null,"published_at":"2019-12-09T20:41:26Z","last_edited_at":"2020-06-24T20:43:18Z","original_locale":"en-US","languages":["en"],"language_details":{},"title":"Protect our kids: Florida legislation is moving on the High School Athlete Safety Bill","description":"\u003cp>My name is Laurie Martin-Giordano and my son, Zach suffered an Exertional Heat Stroke (EHS) during summer conditioning workouts for football in 2017. He fought incredibly hard for 11 days, but he could not survive his devastating injuries. I had to plan my 16 year old son's funeral. In the weeks after his death, I began to research exertional heat stroke and I learned a few things that crushed my already broken heart:\u003c/p>\n\u003col>\n\u003cli>EHS is preventable simply by recognizing the early symptoms of heat illness (dizziness, vomiting) and removing the person from the activity to a cooler area, away from the sun.\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>100% of EHS victims survive when Cold Water Immersion (CWI) is used promptly, on-site.\u003c/li>\n\u003c/ol>\n\u003cp>CWI wasn't used to treat Zach, but why not? Florida high school athletes, cheerleaders, band members, and JROTC all traditionally participate in summer conditioning workouts. I learned that any rules and policies, set up by the Florida High School Athletic Association (FHSAA) to ensure their kids' safety, ONLY apply during the academic school year. The guidelines for response to cardiac arrest and heat illness, 2 of the 3 most common reasons for sudden death of high school kids, are only suggestions. (Football practice for two weeks prior to school starting in the Fall is included as \"pre-season\" with a few specific rules.)\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>All attempts over the last 2 years by me, along with heat illness experts, Athletic Trainers, and FHSAA's own Medical Advisory Board, to change the handbook suggestions to mandatory policies have been voted down by the FHSAA Board. This week, Legislators in the FL House of Representatives have a bill to vote on that incorporates \"best practice\" safety measures to protect our kids, including the use of AED's, Wet Bulb Globe Thermometer temperature activity modification guidelines and using Cold Water Immersion to treat EHS.\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>By signing this petition, you are voicing your support of the proposed sports safety bill that will be discussed and believe this legislation will save lives, and is necessary to provide leadership to our schools in regard to sports safety. \u003c/p>","targeting_description":"Ralph E. Massullo, MD, Keith Perry, Janet Cruz, Lizbeth Benacquisto, Bill Montford, Kathleen Passidomo, Ron DeSantis, Delores D. Hogan Johnson, Thad Altman, Fentrice Driskell, Heather Fitzenhagen, ...","letter_body":"Ask Governor DeSantis to sign the Zachary Martin Act (Florida Athlete Safety SB1696/HB7011) into law.\n\nI am writing this letter regarding the athlete safety bill which was favorably and unanimously voted for by the Florida House and Senate during the 2019-2020 legislative session. I fully believe this legislation will save lives and is necessary to provide leadership to our schools regarding sports safety.  Heat stroke is 100% preventable if we are properly prepared. Additionally, victims of Exertional Heat Stroke that are given immediate, on-site Cold Water Immersion treatment have 100% survival rate.\n\nLaurie Martin-Giordano is the mother of Zach Martin, a 16 year old young man who died from Exertional Heat Stroke at a Florida high school in 2017. She has put forth great effort to protect high school athletes with mandatory safety guidelines since her son's death. The language in this bill reflects recommendations to the FHSAA, which have been passed today (6/9/20) by their Board of Directors, pending the Zachary Martin Act becoming Florida law. \n\nDue to the COVID-19 pandemic, Florida residents were asked to stay home, and schools switched to online learning formats. High school sports and related activities were canceled. While athletes have made efforts to continue their physical training, most have not been able to continue at the same intensity required at in-person group workouts.\n\nThe current phased reopening of Florida by Governor DeSantis allows high school sports to begin in-person summer conditioning now. While the start date for the Zachary Martin Act requirements is July 1, 2020, the mandates are written to protect these kids, and specifically include summer conditioning, a protection not previously required by FHSAA, nor practiced by a number of high schools. \n\nStarting kids back to intense, outdoor conditioning in Florida heat and humidity after 3 months of rest in air conditioned homes is a recipe for disaster. Even if someone does not die from Sudden Cardiac Arrest or Exertional Heat Stroke, they can have injuries that impact them the rest of their lives. They need the protection given by the Zachary Martin Act.\n\nI want you to know that this bill has my full support to provide \"best practice\" standards for the health and safety of Florida’s young people. \n\nFlorida House and Senate members, please present this bill to Governor DeSantis as it is urgently needed. \nGovernor DeSantis, please sign the Zachary Martin Act into law as soon as possible to protect our     <script>
      (function() {
        var spinnerActionButton;
        function getFirstElementByClassName(className) {
          var elementsByClassName = document.getElementsByClassName(className);
          if (!elementsByClassName || !elementsByClassName.length) return;
          return elementsByClassName[0];
        }

        function showActionButtonSpinner(e) {
          var spinnerButton = getFirstElementByClassName('js-action-button-spinner');
          if (!spinnerButton) return;
          e.target.className += ' hide-fully';
          spinnerButton.className = spinnerButton.className.replace('hide-fully', '');
          window.preLoadActionButtonClick = true;
        }

        spinnerActionButton = getFirstElementByClassName('js-action-button-preload-click-spinner');
        if (spinnerActionButton) {
          spinnerActionButton.addEventListener('click', showActionButtonSpinner);
        }

        window.removePreBundleEvents = function() {
          if (spinnerActionButton) spinnerActionButton.removeEventListener('click', showActionButtonSpinner);
        }
      })();
    </script>
  </body>

</html>
